Inclusion of the Second Limit (Ghayah) in Talaq: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explaining the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on ghayah inclusion in talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on inclusion of the second limit (ghayah) in talaq expressions and explain the basis for the disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In talaq, the second limit is not included because talaq is a matter of risk, not permissibility.

When a husband says 'you are talaq from one to two' or 'from one to three', how many talaqs actually fall? This depends on whether the second number (ghayah) is included. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on this point. The dispute hinges on the role of customary usage ('urf) in matters of risk versus permissibility. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression and the two limits
Take the phrase 'from one to two' or 'from one to three'. The first limit is 'one', the second limit is 'two' or 'three'. Determine what the speaker intends literally.
In Arabic, 'إلى' (to) can be inclusive or exclusive of the end point depending on context.
2
State Abu Hanifa's rule
Abu Hanifa holds that only the first limit is included. The second limit is excluded unless necessary. So 'from one to two' gives one talaq; 'from one to three' gives two talaqs. Reason: talaq is a matter of risk (khatar), where custom does not include the end limit.
This is the default position in the matn of Al-Kanz.
3
State the Sahibayn's rule
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say both limits are included by istihsan (juristic preference) based on customary usage ('urf). So 'from one to two' gives two talaqs; 'from one to three' gives three.
They consider that people generally include both ends in such expressions.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa distinguishes matters of permissibility (ibaha) from matters of risk (khatar). Custom includes the second limit only in permissibility matters (like buying, eating). Talaq is a risk, so custom does not apply. The Sahibayn argue that custom is the default unless there is a qarina (indication) to the contrary; here the wording itself suggests inclusion.
The author explains that the first limit must be included because the second talaq cannot occur without the first. The second limit is not needed for the occurrence of the second talaq.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the number of talaq: under Abu Hanifa fewer talaqs fall, under Sahibayn more. This determines whether the marriage becomes irrevocably dissolved (three talaqs) or remains revocable after one or two.
For example, 'from one to three' under Sahibayn results in three talaqs, making remarriage impossible without halala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن واحدة أو ما بين واحدة إلى ثنتين واحدة وإلى ثلاث ثنتان) يعني عند أبي حنيفة فتدخل الغاية الأولى دون الثانية، وقالا بدخولهما فيقع في الأولى ثنتان وفي الثانية ثلاث استحساناً بالتعارف إلا أنهما أطلقا فيه وأبو حنيفة يقول : إنما تدخل الغايتان عرفاً فيما مرجعه الإباحة كخذ من مالي من عشرة إلى مائة وبع عبدي بمال من مائة إلى ألف، وكل من الملح إلى الحلو فله أخذ المائة والبيع بألف وأكل الحلواء، وأما ما أصله الخطر حتى يباح إلا لدفع الحاجة ،فلا والطلاق منه فكان قرينة على عدم إرادة الكل غير أن الغاية الأولى لا بد من وجودها ليرتب عليها الطلقة الثانية في صورة إيقاعها وهي صورة من واحدة إلى ثلاث إذ لا ثانية بلا أولى ووجود الطلاق عين وقوعه بخلاف الغاية الثانية وهي ثلاث في هذه الصورة فإنه يصح وقوع الثانية بلا ،ثالثة أما صورة من واحدة إلى ثنتين فلا حاجة إلى إدخالها لأنها إنما دخلت ضرورة إيقاع الثانية وهو منتف وإيقاع الواحدة ليس باعتبار إدخالها غاية بل بما ذكرنا من انتفاء العرف فيه فلا تدخل فيلغو قوله من واحدة إلى ثنتين ويقع بطالق واحدة ولا يرد أنت طالق ثانية حيث لا يقع إلا واحدة لأن ثانية لغو فيقع بأنت طالق. وقد ظهر بهذا التقرير أن الاختلاف إنما نشأ من اعتبار إثبات العرف وعدمه مع الاتفاق على اعتبار العرف فلا يرد دخول المرافق لأن العرف لما أدخل ما بعد إلى تارة وأخرجه أخرى وكان الاحتياط الدخول فإن قيل : ما بين هذا وهذا يستدعي وجود الأمرين ووجودهما وقوعهما فيقع الثلاث الجواب أن ذلك في المحسوسات، وأما ما نحن فيه من الأمور المعنوية فإنما يقتضي الأول احتمال وجود الثاني عرفاً، ففيما بين الستين إلى السبعين يصدق إذا لم يبلغ السبعين. كذا في فتح القدير. وفي جامع الفصولين : لو باع بالخيار إلى غد دخل الغد في الخيار ، ولو حلف ليقضين دينه إلى خمسة أيام لا يحنث ما لم تغرب الشمس من اليوم الخامس، وكذا لا يكلمه إلى عشرة أيام دخل العاشر وكذا في إن تزوجت إلى عشر سنين دخلت العاشرة، وأما في الإجازة ففي بعض الكتب : لو أجر إلى خمس سنين دخلت الخامسة، وفي عامة الكتب لا تدخل ا هـ . و تمام تقريره في شرحنا المسمى بتعليق الأنوار على أصول المنار. ولو نوى في الثانية واحدة دين ديانة لا قضاء لأنه يحتمله وهو خلاف الظاهر. وأشار بقوله إلى ثنتين إلى أنه لو قال من واحدة إلى واحدة تقع واحدة بالأولى اتفاقاً، وقيل أعني من واحدة إلى ثلاث أو ما بين واحدة إلى ثلاث قوله : (وقيل لا يقع شيء عند زفر) أي في قوله من واحدة إلى واحدة .
His statement: 'And from one, or from between one to two, one, and to three, two' means according to Abu Hanifa: the first limit is included and not the second, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said both are included, so in the first case two fall and in the second three fall, by istihsan based on customary usage, except that they made it absolute. Abu Hanifa says: the two limits are only included customarily in matters whose origin is permissibility, like 'take from my property from ten to one hundred' and 'sell my slave for a price from one hundred to one thousand' and 'eat from salt to sweet', so he may take the hundred, sell for a thousand, and eat the sweet. As for matters whose origin is danger, not permissible except to repel need, it is not like that, and talaq is from this, so it is a qarina (indicative) of not intending the whole. However, the first limit must exist for the second talaq to be built upon it in the case of its occurrence, which is the case of 'from one to three', since there is no second without a first, and the existence of talaq is its occurrence itself, unlike the second limit which is three in this case, because the occurrence of the second is valid without a third. As for the case of 'from one to two', there is no need to include it because it is only included due to the necessity of the occurrence of the second, and that is absent, and the occurrence of one is not by virtue of including it as a limit but by what we mentioned of the absence of custom, so it is not included, and his statement 'from one to two' becomes لغوا (void), and one talaq falls by 'taliq wahida'. And it is not objected: 'You are talaq a second' where only one falls because 'second' is لغوا, so it falls by 'anta taliq'. And from this exposition it is clear that the disagreement arose from considering the establishment of custom or not, while agreeing on considering custom, so the objection of including bathrooms does not arise, because custom sometimes includes what is after 'to' and sometimes excludes it, and precaution is inclusion. If it is said: 'What is between this and that necessitates the existence of both, and their existence is their occurrence, so three falls', the answer is that this is in physical matters, but in what we are discussing from conceptual matters, the first only necessitates the possibility of the second by custom, so in 'between sixty and seventy' it is true if he does not reach seventy. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in Jami' al-Fusulain: If he sold with an option until tomorrow, tomorrow enters the option; if he swore to pay his debt within five days, he does not break his oath until the sun sets on the fifth day; similarly 'he will not speak to him for ten days' includes the tenth; likewise in 'if I marry within ten years' includes the tenth. As for rental: in some books: if he rents for five years, the fifth enters; in most books it does not enter. And the complete explanation is in our commentary called Ta'liq al-Anwar 'ala Usul al-Manar. And if he intended in the second one [talaq], it is believed in the religious sense, not judicially, because it is possible and contrary to the apparent. And he indicated by his statement 'to two' that if he said 'from one to one', one falls by the first, by agreement. And it was said: I mean from one to three or from between one to three. His statement: 'And it was said: nothing falls according to Zufar' i.e., in his statement 'from one to one'.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the inclusion of the second limit (ghayah) when a husband says 'from one to two' or 'from one to three' in talaq. Abu Hanifa holds that only the first limit (the start) is included, so 'from one to two' yields one talaq (only the first), and 'from one to three' yields two talaqs (one and two, but three is not included). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say both limits are included by istihsan based on customary usage ('urf), so 'from one to two' yields two, and 'from one to three' yields three. The author explains the reasoning: custom includes the second limit only in matters of permissibility (mubah), like buying or eating where the limit is meant inclusively. Talaq is a matter of risk (khatar), so custom does not include the upper limit as a qarina (indication) that the speaker did not intend the full range. The first limit must be included because without it the second talaq could not occur. The author also discusses the case of 'from one to one' where there is agreement that one talaq falls by the first number. Zufar, however, says nothing falls in 'from one to one' because no talaq is specified, but the author notes the correct view is that one talaq falls and 'one' after 'to' is لغو. The passage also mentions that if the husband intended one in the second, he is believed religiously (dinan) but not judicially (qada'an).

Key Terms
غاية (ghayah): The end limit of a number or time period mentioned after the word 'to' (إلى). In this context, it refers to the second number in 'from one to two'.
لغو (laghw): Void, meaningless; a word that has no legal effect because it is redundant or contradictory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a husband says 'you are talaq from one to two', how many talaqs fall?
A) One talaq
B) Two talaqs
C) Three talaqs
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi talaq, the second limit (ghayah) is not included because talaq is a matter of risk, not permissibility, contra the Sahibayn's istihsan based on custom.

Ruling on 'From One to Ten' and 'From Three to One' in Talaq
Ruling on 'min wahidah ila ashara' and 'min thalath ila wahidah' with ijma claim and internal ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the talaq expressions 'min wahidah ila ashara' and 'min thalath ila wahidah', and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the number of talaqs.

Core Idea
When the wording of talaq is explicit, the number of talaqs is determined by the wording, not by the wife's request.

In this lesson, we examine two specific numeric talaq expressions: 'from one to ten' and 'from three to one'. The Hanafi school holds that the wording of the husband is paramount, leading to a ruling of three talaqs in both cases. However, there is an internal difference: Abu Hanifa considered that 'from one to ten' results in two talaqs, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it is three. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes that the relied-upon view is three, citing consensus and the principle that wording is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expressions
Note the two phrases: 'min wahidah ila ashara' (from one to ten) and 'min thalath ila wahidah' (from three to one). Both are attempts to specify a range of talaq numbers.
The first expression is ambiguous: does it mean one talaq in each of ten times, or a total of ten? The Hanafi school interprets it as three talaqs.
2
Understand the ijma claim
The author states 'three by consensus' (ثلاث بالإجماع) because the wording is considered (اللفظ معتبر) in talaq. This 'consensus' is the preferred view within the Hanafi school, not absolute universal consensus.
The exemplar given: if the wife asks for six talaqs for 1000, and the husband says three talaqs, only three fall because the wording overrides her request.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The author then reveals that there is a difference: according to Abu Hanifa, two talaqs fall (عنده ثنتان), while according to the Sahibayn, three fall (عندها ثلاث). This is an intra-madhhab dispute.
The pronoun 'عندها' likely refers to the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who form the majority of the school.
4
Analyze the exemplar
The exemplar of 'six for one thousand' shows that the husband's words are given weight: if he says three, only three count, even if she asked for six. This reinforces the principle that wording (اللفظ) is the determinant.
The price (five hundred) is calculated proportionally: half of the agreed amount, since half the number of talaqs was given.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author prefaces with 'وقيل' (it was said) indicating that the consensus view is not absolute. However, the preferred view, as cited from al-Qunyah, is that three talaqs occur, because wording is paramount. This is the relied-upon fatwa position.
The phrase 'وينبغي أن يكون هذا بالاتفاق' suggests that the author initially thought it was agreed, but later noted the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقيل ثلاث بالإجماع لأن اللفظ معتبر في الطلاق حتى لو قالت طلقني ستاً بألف فطلقها ثلاثاً وقعن بخمسمائة. ورجحه في القنية بأنه أحسن من حيث المعنى وفيها : لو قال أنت طالق من ثلاث إلى واحدة تقع ثلاث. قال رحمه الله تعالى : وينبغي أن يكون هذا بالاتفاق. ثم ظهر لي أنه على قولهما وهو منصوص عليه في بعض الكتب أنه يقع عنده ثنتان وعندها ثلاث ا هـ . بديع قوله : (وواحدة في ثنتين واحدة إن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى الضرب) أي تقع واحدة فيما لو قال أنت طالق واحدة في ثنتين إن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى الضرب والحساب عالماً بعرف الحساب خلافاً لزفر في الثاني لأن عرفهم فيه تضعيف أحد العددين بعدد الآخر كقوله واحد مرتين. ولنا أن قوله في ثنتين ظرف حقيقة وهو لا يصلح له فيقع المظروف دون الظرف ولهذا لزمه «له عشرة في علي عشرة في عشرة إلا إن قصد المعية أو العطف فعشرون لمناسبة الظرف كليهما. وأما الضرب فإن كان في الممسوحات أعني فيما له طول وعرض وعمق فأثره في تكثير المضروب، وإذا كان فيما ليس له طول وعرض فأثره في تكثير الأجزاء فإنه لو زاد بالضرب في نفسه لم يبق أحد في الدنيا فقيراً لأنه يضرب ما ملكه من الدراهم في مائة فيصير المائة مائة، ثم يضرب في الألف فيصير مائة ألف فصار معنى قولنا واحدة في ثنتين واحدة ذو جزأين، وكذا قولنا واحدة في ثلاث واحدة ذو أجزاء ثلاثة والتطليقة الواحدة وإن كثرت أجزاؤها لا تصير أكثر من واحدة. كذا في المعراج. ورجح في فتح القدير والتحرير قول زفر بأن الكلام في عرف الحساب في التركيب اللفظي كون أحد العددين مضعفاً . الآخر، والعرف لا يمنع، والفرض أنه تكلم بعرفهم وأراده فصار كما لو أوقع بلغة أخرى فارسية أو غيرها وهو يدريها ا.هـ. وهكذا رجحه في غاية البيان وجوابه أن اللفظ لما لم يكن صالحاً له لم يعتبر فيه العرف ولا النية كما لو نوى بقوله اسقني الماء الطلاق فإنه لا يقع به
His statement: 'And it was said: three by consensus, because the wording is considered in talaq, such that if she said 'divorce me six times for one thousand' and he divorced her three times, they fall for five hundred.' And he preferred it in al-Qunyah because it is better in terms of meaning. And in it: if he said 'you are talaq from three to one', three fall. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'It should be that this is by agreement. Then it appeared to me that it is according to their statement, and it is stated in some books that according to him two fall, and according to her three fall.' Badi'. His statement: 'And one in two is one if he did not intend anything or intended multiplication' i.e., one talaq falls if he said 'you are talaq one in two' if he did not intend anything or intended multiplication and arithmetic, being aware of the custom of arithmetic, contrary to Zufar in the second, because their custom in it is to multiply one number by the other, like saying 'one twice'. For us, his statement 'in two' is literally a container and it is not suitable for him, so the contained falls without the container, and for this reason, if someone has ten in 'ali' ten in ten, unless he intends concomitance or conjunction, then twenty due to the suitability of both containers. As for multiplication, if it is in measured things i.e., having length, width, and depth, its effect is to multiply the multiplicand; and if it is something without length and width, its effect is to multiply parts; if one increased by multiplying itself, no one in the world would be poor. So the meaning of our saying 'one in two' is one possessing two parts, and similarly our saying 'one in three' is one possessing three parts, and a single talaq even if its parts are many does not become more than one. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir, the view of Zufar was preferred: that speech in the custom of arithmetic in verbal composition is that one of the two numbers multiplies the other, and custom is not prevented, and it is presumed that he spoke according to their custom and intended it, so it becomes as if he expressed it in another language like Persian or other which he knows. Similarly, it was preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan. And its answer: that the wording, since it is not suitable for it, custom and intention are not considered, as if he intended by saying 'give me water' talaq, it does not fall by it.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage contains additional rulings and a hashiah (marginal comment) on previous material. The first part discusses the expression 'from one to ten'. It is reported that by consensus (ijma') three talaqs occur, because the wording is given weight in talaq. An example: if the wife says 'divorce me six times for one thousand' and he divorces her three times, they count as three for five hundred. This is preferred in al-Qunyah. Then the passage discusses 'from three to one': it is said that three fall, and the author notes that according to Abu Hanifa two fall and according to the Sahibayn three fall, but the relied-upon view is three by agreement? The hashiah then re-mentions the 'one in two' dispute, giving Zufar's view and the Hanafi response. However, the core of this lesson is the ruling on 'from one to ten' and 'from three to one' with the ijma' claim. The hashiah serves as a critical refinement of the previous lesson's 'one in two' issue, reaffirming the Hanafi position despite later preferences for Zufar.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus; here it means the preferred view of the Hanafi school, not absolute consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, how many talaqs occur when a husband says 'you are talaq from three to one'?
A) One talaq
B) Two talaqs
C) Three talaqs
D) No talaq

Key Takeaway
When a husband uses an ambiguous numeric talaq expression like 'from one to ten' or 'from three to one', the ruling is three talaqs because the wording is given priority over the wife's request or the husband's intention.

The 'One in Two' Dispute: Multiplication vs Container Interpretation
Hashiah on 'one in two' dispute between Hanafi literal view and Zufar's multiplication view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that custom ('urf) is considered only if the wording is ambiguous, by analyzing the 'one in two' talaq expression and contrasting the Hanafi container interpretation with Zufar's multiplication interpretation.

Core Idea
In talaq, 'one in two' means one talaq with parts, not two talaqs, because 'in' is a container preposition, not a multiplication operator.

This lesson examines the controversial expression 'one in two' (واحدة في ثنتين) in talaq. The Hanafi school takes the word 'in' (في) literally as a container preposition, resulting in one talaq that is divisible into two parts. However, the Hanafi scholar Zufar argued that in arithmetic custom, 'in' means multiplication, so 'one in two' should be two talaqs. The hashiah from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the debate and shows that despite later preponderance of Zufar's view in some texts, the established Hanafi position is that wording prevails over custom when the wording is clear.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
A husband says 'you are talaq one in two' (واحدة في ثنتين). The question is how many talaqs occur: one or two?
The wording is ambiguous: 'in' could mean multiplication (as in 'one times two') or container (as in 'one contained in two').
2
Explain the Hanafi container interpretation
The Hanafi position (from the matn) is that it is one talaq if no intention or multiplication is intended. The reasoning: 'in two' is literally a container (ظرف) that does not fit as a container for a talaq; thus the contained (one) falls validly while the container (two) is ignored.
The analogy given: 'he has ten in 'ali' (عشرة في علي) means ten is possessed by 'ali, not multiplied. Similarly, one talaq 'in two' means one talaq with two characteristics or parts.
3
Understand Zufar's multiplication custom argument
Zufar argues that in the custom of mathematicians, 'one in two' means one times two, i.e., two. Since the husband spoke in an arithmetic context (he knew the custom), his intention should be considered.
Some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., in Fath al-Qadir, al-Tahrir) preferred Zufar's view, equating it to speaking a foreign language where custom governs.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The wording 'in two' is not suitable for the meaning of multiplication; therefore, neither custom nor intention can change the literal meaning. An example: if someone says 'give me water' intending talaq, it does not occur because the wording does not fit talaq.
The key principle: the wording must be valid (salih) for the intended meaning; if it is not, custom and intention are irrelevant.
5
Determine the ruling and its basis
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is one talaq, because the wording is taken literally and does not support multiplication. The commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq follows this view, despite noting that some later scholars preferred Zufar.
The student should understand that the Hanafi school gives priority to the linguistic literal meaning over customary usage when the wording is unambiguous in its literal sense.

Source Text

قوله : (وقيل ثلاث بالإجماع لأن اللفظ معتبر في الطلاق حتى لو قالت طلقني ستاً بألف فطلقها ثلاثاً وقعن بخمسمائة. ورجحه في القنية بأنه أحسن من حيث المعنى وفيها : لو قال أنت طالق من ثلاث إلى واحدة تقع ثلاث. قال رحمه الله تعالى : وينبغي أن يكون هذا بالاتفاق. ثم ظهر لي أنه على قولهما وهو منصوص عليه في بعض الكتب أنه يقع عنده ثنتان وعندها ثلاث ا هـ . بديع قوله : (وواحدة في ثنتين واحدة إن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى الضرب) أي تقع واحدة فيما لو قال أنت طالق واحدة في ثنتين إن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى الضرب والحساب عالماً بعرف الحساب خلافاً لزفر في الثاني لأن عرفهم فيه تضعيف أحد العددين بعدد الآخر كقوله واحد مرتين. ولنا أن قوله في ثنتين ظرف حقيقة وهو لا يصلح له فيقع المظروف دون الظرف ولهذا لزمه «له عشرة في علي عشرة في عشرة إلا إن قصد المعية أو العطف فعشرون لمناسبة الظرف كليهما. وأما الضرب فإن كان في الممسوحات أعني فيما له طول وعرض وعمق فأثره في تكثير المضروب، وإذا كان فيما ليس له طول وعرض فأثره في تكثير الأجزاء فإنه لو زاد بالضرب في نفسه لم يبق أحد في الدنيا فقيراً لأنه يضرب ما ملكه من الدراهم في مائة فيصير المائة مائة، ثم يضرب في الألف فيصير مائة ألف فصار معنى قولنا واحدة في ثنتين واحدة ذو جزأين، وكذا قولنا واحدة في ثلاث واحدة ذو أجزاء ثلاثة والتطليقة الواحدة وإن كثرت أجزاؤها لا تصير أكثر من واحدة. كذا في المعراج. ورجح في فتح القدير والتحرير قول زفر بأن الكلام في عرف الحساب في التركيب اللفظي كون أحد العددين مضعفاً . الآخر، والعرف لا يمنع، والفرض أنه تكلم بعرفهم وأراده فصار كما لو أوقع بلغة أخرى فارسية أو غيرها وهو يدريها ا.هـ. وهكذا رجحه في غاية البيان وجوابه أن اللفظ لما لم يكن صالحاً له لم يعتبر فيه العرف ولا النية كما لو نوى بقوله اسقني الماء الطلاق فإنه لا يقع به
His statement: 'And it was said: three by consensus, because the wording is considered in talaq, such that if she said 'divorce me six times for one thousand' and he divorced her three times, they fall for five hundred.' And he preferred it in al-Qunyah because it is better in terms of meaning. And in it: if he said 'you are talaq from three to one', three fall. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'It should be that this is by agreement. Then it appeared to me that it is according to their statement, and it is stated in some books that according to him two fall, and according to her three fall.' Badi'. His statement: 'And one in two is one if he did not intend anything or intended multiplication' i.e., one talaq falls if he said 'you are talaq one in two' if he did not intend anything or intended multiplication and arithmetic, being aware of the custom of arithmetic, contrary to Zufar in the second, because their custom in it is to multiply one number by the other, like saying 'one twice'. For us, his statement 'in two' is literally a container and it is not suitable for him, so the contained falls without the container, and for this reason, if someone has ten in 'ali' ten in ten, unless he intends concomitance or conjunction, then twenty due to the suitability of both containers. As for multiplication, if it is in measured things i.e., having length, width, and depth, its effect is to multiply the multiplicand; and if it is something without length and width, its effect is to multiply parts; if one increased by multiplying itself, no one in the world would be poor. So the meaning of our saying 'one in two' is one possessing two parts, and similarly our saying 'one in three' is one possessing three parts, and a single talaq even if its parts are many does not become more than one. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir, the view of Zufar was preferred: that speech in the custom of arithmetic in verbal composition is that one of the two numbers multiplies the other, and custom is not prevented, and it is presumed that he spoke according to their custom and intended it, so it becomes as if he expressed it in another language like Persian or other which he knows. Similarly, it was preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan. And its answer: that the wording, since it is not suitable for it, custom and intention are not considered, as if he intended by saying 'give me water' talaq, it does not fall by it.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage contains additional rulings and a hashiah (marginal comment) on previous material. The first part discusses the expression 'from one to ten'. It is reported that by consensus (ijma') three talaqs occur, because the wording is given weight in talaq. An example: if the wife says 'divorce me six times for one thousand' and he divorces her three times, they count as three for five hundred. This is preferred in al-Qunyah. Then the passage discusses 'from three to one': it is said that three fall, and the author notes that according to Abu Hanifa two fall and according to the Sahibayn three fall, but the relied-upon view is three by agreement? The hashiah then re-mentions the 'one in two' dispute, giving Zufar's view and the Hanafi response. However, the core of this lesson is the ruling on 'from one to ten' and 'from three to one' with the ijma' claim. The hashiah serves as a critical refinement of the previous lesson's 'one in two' issue, reaffirming the Hanafi position despite later preferences for Zufar.

Key Terms
الظرف (al-zarf): Container; in grammar, a word indicating time or place ('in', 'on', etc.).
العرف (al-'urf): Custom; prevalent usage in a community or field.
الضرب (al-darb): Multiplication; arithmetic operation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on 'one in two' (واحدة في ثنتين) when the husband intends multiplication?
A) Two talaqs, because of arithmetic custom.
B) One talaq, because the wording 'in' is a container.
C) Three talaqs, as default for ambiguous expressions.
D) The husband's intention is considered, so it depends on his ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi talaq, the literal meaning of words takes precedence over custom and intention, so 'one in two' is one talaq, not two.

Place-Based Talaq Phrases: Immediate Effect
Commentary on place-based talaq phrases with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that place-based talaq phrases result in immediate divorce and explain the qiyas reasoning that talaq is tied to time not place.

Core Idea
Place words in talaq do not delay or extend divorce; it occurs immediately upon utterance.

When a husband says 'you are divorced from here to Syria' or 'in Mecca', does the divorce spread across that region? The Hanafi school clarifies that such phrases are ineffective; the divorce occurs instantly. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind this ruling, grounded in the analogy (qiyas) between talaq and actions which are temporal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrases and their apparent implication
Locate the place-based expressions in the text: 'from here to Syria', 'in Mecca', 'in the house', etc. Note that they seem to condition or locate the divorce, but the ruling states they are immediate (tanzeez).
These are spatial references, not temporal conditions.
2
Understand the reasoning: talaq is an action, actions are temporal
The text explains that talaq has the meaning of an action. Actions occur in time because they have no permanence; they begin and end. Place, by contrast, has permanence. Thus, talaq is more specifically linked to time than to place.
Qiyas: talaq is analogized to all actions, which are inherently time-bound.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The evidence is an analogy (qiyas): talaq is an act; acts are transient like time; place is enduring. Since the ruling of talaq is instantaneous, mentioning a place does not alter its timing. The text cites al-Mi'raj for this principle.
The dalil is aqli (rational) – no explicit text is quoted.
4
Distinguish between religious (diyaanatan) and judicial (qadaa'an) enforcement
If the husband claims he intended a condition (e.g., 'when you wear that garment'), he is believed religiously but not in court. This is analogous to the issue of entry in the book (mas'alat al-dakhul).
Judicially, the divorce is immediate unless proven otherwise.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a husband saying 'you are divorced in the shade' or 'you are divorced in this garment'. According to the text, these are immediate regardless of the wife's actual location or attire.
Place phrases never create suspended talaq (ta'liq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن هنا إلى الشام واحدة) وصفه بالقصر لأن الطلاق متى وقع وقع في جميع الدنيا وفي السموات فلم يثبت بهذا اللفظ زيادة شدة. وقال التمرتاشي : مع أنه إنما مد المرأة لا الطلاق. ووجهه أنه حال ولا يصلح صاحب الحال في التركيب إلا الضمير في طالق . قوله : (وبمكة وفي مكة وفي الدار تنجيز فتطلق في الحال وإن لم يكن في الدار ولا بمكة، وكذا في الظل، وفي الشمس والثوب كالمكان فلو قال في ثوب كذا وعليها غيره طلقت للحال، وكذا لو قال أنت طالق مريضة أو مصلية أو وأنت مريضة، وإن قال عنيت إذا لبست أو إذا مرضت صدق ديانة لا قضاء لما فيه من التخفيف على نفسه كما إذا قصد بمسألة الكتاب الدخول فيتعلق به ديانة لا قضاء وإنما تعلق الطلاق بالزمان دون المكان لأن فيه معنى الفعل وبين الفعل والزمان مناسبة من حيث إنه لا بقاء لهما، فكما يوجدان يذهبان وللمكان بقاء لا يتجدد كل ساعة أما الزمان يتجدد ويحدث كل ساعة كالفعل فكان اختصاص الطلاق بالزمان أكثر . كذا في المعراج
His statement: (and from here to Syria is one) describes it as limited because when divorce occurs, it occurs in the whole world and in the heavens, so no increased severity is established by this wording. And al-Tamartashi said: Although it describes the woman, not the divorce. Its explanation is that it is a state and the owner of the state in the construction is only the pronoun in 'taliq'. His statement: (and 'in Mecca' and 'in Mecca' and 'in the house' are immediate, so she is divorced immediately even if she is not in the house or in Mecca; similarly, 'in the shade' and 'in the sun' and 'the garment' are like a place; if he says 'in such a garment while she wears another', she is divorced immediately; similarly, if he says 'you are divorced sick or praying or while you are sick', and if he says 'I meant when you wear or when you fall sick', he is believed religiously but not judicially, because of the leniency for himself, just as when he intended by the issue of the book entry, it is attached religiously but not judicially. Divorce attaches to time rather than place because there is the meaning of action in it, and between action and time there is suitability in that they both have no permanence; as they exist, they go, while place has permanence that is renewed every hour, but time renews and occurs every hour like action, so divorce is more specific to time. Thus in al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage addresses divorce phrases that mention places, like 'from here to Syria' or 'in Mecca'. The commentator clarifies that such phrases do not restrict or extend the divorce; rather, divorce occurs immediately upon utterance, regardless of location. The reasoning is that divorce is an action that occurs in time, not in place. Actions are temporal and transient, while places are permanent. Therefore, mentioning a place does not affect the timing or validity of the divorce. For example, saying 'you are divorced in Mecca' results in immediate divorce even if the wife is not in Mecca. Similarly, if the husband says 'you are divorced when you are sick' but intends a condition, it is considered a religious intention but not enforceable in court. The key principle is that talaq is tied to time, not place.

Key Terms
التنجيز (al-tanjeez): Immediate effect; the divorce occurs at the moment of utterance without suspension.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspension of divorce on a future condition; here, place words do not create ta'liq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately
B) When she goes to Makkah
C) It does not occur
D) At the end of the year

Key Takeaway
Place-based talaq phrases do not condition or delay divorce; the Hanafi school rules immediate talaq based on the temporal nature of actions.

The Five Meanings of 'Fi' in Divorce and Their Effect on the Number of Divorces
Author explains the five meanings of 'fi' in divorce with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five possible meanings of 'fi' in divorce and apply them to determine the number of divorces in the phrase 'thintayn fi thintayn'.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'fi' in divorce can mean 'and' or 'with', changing the divorce count to three if intended.

The particle 'fi' (في) is common in divorce pronouncements, but its legal effect depends on the husband's intention. While its default meaning is 'in' (ẓarf), the Hanafi school acknowledges that it can also carry the meanings of 'and' (waw) or 'with' (ma'a), leading to different counts of divorces. In this lesson, we examine the five aspects of 'fi' as explained by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, with Quranic evidence supporting the permissibility of the 'with' meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its default meaning
Recognize that 'fi' is a particle of ẓarf (container). Its default legal effect is that no additional divorce is implied; the phrase 'two in two' means two divorces.
2
Understand the role of intention (niyyah)
The husband's intention can change the meaning of 'fi' to conjunction (waw) or accompaniment (ma'a). This changes the count of divorces. The author restricts this to cases where the husband explicitly intends one of these meanings.
If no intention, default applies.
3
List the five aspects (wujuh) of 'fi'
The five aspects are: (1) no intention, (2) intending ẓarf (container), (3) intending ḍarb (to strike), (4) intending waw (and), (5) intending ma'a (with). The first three yield the same ruling – the number stated; the last two add divorces.
The author mentions that ḍarb is mentioned elsewhere; here it is included for completeness.
4
Apply to the example 'thintayn fi thintayn'
If the husband says to his consummated wife 'you are divorced two in two' with no intention or intending ẓarf/ḍarb, the result is two divorces. If he intends waw (and) or ma'a (with), it becomes three divorces (because two plus two would be four, but the maximum of three applies).
For an unconsummated wife, the maximum is two, so the result differs.
5
Examine the Quranic proof for the 'with' meaning
The author cites the verse 'wa yatajāwazu 'an sayyi'ātihim fī aṣḥābi al-jannah' (al-Ahqaf 46:16) where 'fi' means 'with' (ma'a). This proves that 'fi' can legitimately carry the meaning of accompaniment in Arabic, justifying its application in divorce.
The alternative proof from al-Fajr 29-30 is rejected as weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرف الواو للجمع والظرف يجمع المظروف فصح أن يراد به معنى الواو. وقيد بكونه نوى بـ«في» الواو لأنه لو نوى بها معنى مع وقع الثلاث مدخولاً بها أو غير مدخول بها كما لو قال لغير المدخول بها أنت طالق واحدة مع ثنتين وإرادة معنى لفظة مع» بها ثابت كقوله تعالى ويتجاوز عن سيئاتهم في أصحاب الجنة ) [الأحقاف : ١٦] وأما الاستشهاد بقوله تعالى فادخلي في عبادي) [الفجر: ۲۹] أي مع عبادي فبعيد ينبو عنه وادخلي جنتي [الفجر: ٢٩] فإن دخولها معهم ليس إلا إلى الجنة فهي على حقيقتها، ولهذا قال في الكشاف : إن المراد في جملة عبادي وقيل في أجساد عبادي ويؤيده قراءة «في عبدي» والأوجه الاستشهاد بما ذكرنا، وحكم ما إذا نوى الظرفية حكم ما إذا لم ينو شيئاً لأنه ظرف له فلذا لم يذكره المصنف فالوجوه خمسة قوله: (وثنتين في ثنتين ثنتان يعني إن لم تكن له نية أو نوى الظرف أو الضرب لما ذكرنا وإن نوى معنى الواو أو معنى مع وقعت ثلاث في المدخول بها وفي غيرها ثنتان في الأول وثلاث في الثاني كما قدمناه
The letter waw is for conjunction, and ẓarf combines the contained, so it is correct that by it the meaning of waw is intended. It is restricted to his intending by 'fi' the [meaning of] waw, because if he intends by it the meaning of 'with' (ma'a), three occur whether she is consummated or not, as if he says to an unconsummated wife 'you are divorced one with two'. And the intention of the meaning of the word 'with' (ma'a) is established by His statement 'and He pardons their sins among the companions of Paradise' [al-Ahqaf:16]. As for citing His statement 'Enter among My servants' [al-Fajr:29], i.e., with My servants, it is far-fetched and repelled, and 'enter My Paradise' [al-Fajr:29]—for her entering with them is only into Paradise, so it is in its literal meaning. Hence al-Kashshaf said: the intended meaning is 'among My servants' and it was said 'in the bodies of My servants', and the reading 'in My servant' supports it, but the proper citation is what we mentioned. The ruling when he intends the ẓarf meaning is the same as when he intends nothing, because it is a ẓarf for it, so the author did not mention it. Thus the aspects are five. His statement: 'and two in two [is] two' means if he has no intention or intends ẓarf or [the meaning of] 'to strike' as we mentioned, and if he intends the meaning of waw or the meaning of 'with', three occur for the consummated wife, and for the unconsummated two in the first and three in the second as we previously stated.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. The author explains that the word 'fi' in divorce can carry five different meanings depending on the husband's intention. The base meaning is as a ẓarf (container), which yields the same ruling as having no specific intention. If the husband intends the waw (conjunction) or ma'a (accompaniment), additional divorces result. The proof for the permissibility of using 'fi' to mean 'with' is taken from the Quranic verse 'in the companions of Paradise' meaning 'with the companions'. The author rejects the alternative proof from 'enter among My servants' because the context requires literal interpretation. The five aspects are: no intention, intending ẓarf, intending the meaning of 'to strike' (ḍarb), intending waw, and intending ma'a. The specific example of 'thintayn fi thintayn' is ruled as two divorces if no intention or ẓarf is intended, and three if waw or ma'a is intended in the case of a consummated marriage; for an unconsummated wife, it is two in the first case and three in the second.

Key Terms
في (fi): A particle that can mean 'in' (ẓarf), 'and' (waw), or 'with' (ma'a) depending on intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'And He pardons their sins among the companions of Paradise' (al-Ahqaf 16)
C) 'And enter My Paradise' (al-Fajr 30)
D) 'And He is with you wherever you are'

Key Takeaway
The particle 'fi' in divorce has five possible meanings; the number of divorces depends on the husband's intention, with the default being the ẓarf meaning (no addition).

Ruling on 'From Here to al-Sham' in Divorce
Author explains that specifying a place does not increase the effect of divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband says 'you are divorced from here to al-Sham' and explain why the specification does not increase the effect.

Core Idea
Specifying a place in a divorce does not increase its severity; it remains one revocable divorce.

You might think that adding a phrase like 'from here to al-Sham' makes the divorce more severe or covers more territory. However, the Hanafi rule is clear: divorce already applies universally, so such a specification has no legal effect. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this ruling, including a subtle grammatical point about the word 'ṭāliq'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The husband pronounces talaq with a locative phrase. The ruling is that only one revocable divorce occurs.
The phrase does not change the number or severity.
2
Understand the rationale
Divorce applies everywhere in the world and the heavens; the phrase cannot increase that scope.
The effect of talaq is not limited by geography.
3
Analyze the grammatical point
The word 'ṭāliq' contains a pronoun referring to the woman, so the phrase 'from here to al-Sham' acts as a ḥāl describing her state, not the divorce itself.
Al-Tamartashi clarifies that only the woman is extended, not the talaq.
4
Conclude the consequence
No increase in number or intensity; the divorce remains one and revocable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن هنا إلى الشام واحدة) وصفه بالقصر لأن الطلاق متى وقع وقع في جميع الدنيا وفي السموات فلم يثبت بهذا اللفظ زيادة شدة. وقال التمرتاشي : مع أنه إنما مد المرأة لا الطلاق. ووجهه أنه حال ولا يصلح صاحب الحال في التركيب إلا الضمير في طالق
His statement: 'and from here to al-Sham [is] one' — he described it as restricted because divorce, whenever it occurs, occurs in all the world and in the heavens, so no increase of severity is established by this wording. Al-Tamartashi said: although he only extended the woman, not the divorce. Its justification is that it is a circumstantial accusative (ḥāl), and the owner of the ḥāl in the construction is only the pronoun in 'ṭāliq'.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a brief ruling statement on the effect of specifying a vast geographical area in a divorce pronouncement. The author explains that saying 'you are divorced from here to al-Sham' still results in only one revocable divorce, because divorce already applies everywhere in the world and the heavens. Adding such a specification does not increase the severity or number of divorces. Al-Tamartashi adds that the phrase only describes the woman's status, not the divorce itself; the word 'ṭāliq' contains a pronoun referring to the woman, so the ḥāl (circumstantial accusative) describes her, not the divorce. Thus, no additional effect.

Key Terms
حال (ḥāl): A circumstantial accusative that describes the state of the subject or object, here the pronoun in 'ṭāliq'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Specifying a place in a divorce does not increase its effect; the divorce remains one and revocable.

The Immediate and Conditional Divorce: The Role of the Particle 'في'
Explaining when 'في' indicates immediate vs. conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between immediate (tanjiz) and suspended (ta'liq) divorce based on the object of the particle 'في', and apply the Hanafi rule to various formulations.

Core Idea
When 'في' attaches to an existing place, divorce is immediate; when attached to a future action, it is suspended.

The particle 'في' (in/at/during) can change the timing of a divorce pronouncement. In Hanafi fiqh, the legal effect depends critically on whether what follows 'في' is an existing place (like a house) or a future action (like entering). Understanding this linguistic nuance prevents mistaken legal consequences. This lesson unpacks the rulings from the classical text Bahr al-Ra'iq and its commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object after 'في'
Look at the word immediately following 'في' in the divorce statement. Is it a noun referring to a place (like الدار, مكة) or an action (like دخول, حيض)?
The same analysis applies to phrases like 'فيها' where the pronoun refers back to a previously mentioned place or action.
2
Determine if the object exists now
Classify the object as either an already existing entity (e.g., 'the house') or a future event (e.g., 'your entering'). Existing entities make the divorce immediate; future events make it conditional.
Time phrases like 'ثلاثة أيام' are treated as immediate due to customary usage.
3
Apply the rule: tanjiz or ta'liq
If the object is an existing place, the divorce takes effect immediately upon utterance. If it is a future action, the divorce is suspended until that action occurs.
For actions like illness or prayer, the same principle applies: conditional.
4
Handle special cases: 'فيها' and 'في حيضة'
When 'فيها' appears, the 'ها' refers to the divorce instance, so the suspended condition fails and the divorce becomes immediate. For 'في حيضة', the hadith about istibra' confirms that 'حيضة' means a complete menstruation, so the condition is the completion of one full menstruation and then purity.
The hadith cited uses 'حيضة' to indicate a complete period, not just the onset of blood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب الطلاق

رجعية وبمكة أو في مكة أو في الدار تنجيز وإذا دخلت مكة تعليق . وهو معنى الشرط للمناسبة بينهما، ولو قال أنت طالق فيها دخولك الدار طلقت في الحال. كذا صفة في المحيط والمعراج. وأوضحه في الذخيرة بأنه إذا ذكر «في» بدون حرف الهاء يصير للمذكور أولاً . الطلاق والدخول لا يصلح ظرفاً لأنه فعل فجعل شرطاً فصار الطلاق معلقاً بدخول الدار. وإذا ذكر في مع حرف الهاء صار صفة للمذكور آخراً وهو الدخول والطلاق لا يصلح ظرفاً للدخول ولا يمكن جعل الطلاق شرطاً أيضاً للدخول فتعذر العمل بالظرفية والشرطية فيلغى كلمة (في» فوقع بقوله أنت طالق .اهـ. فإن كانت الرواية بهاء التأنيث فهي راجعة إلى الطلقة وإن كان الضمير مذكراً فهو عائد إلى الطلاق كما لا يخفى. وإنما لا يصح التعليق بها في قوله لأجنبية أنت طالق في نكاحك حتى لو تزوجها لا تقع لأنها كالتعليق توقفاً لا ترتباً وتمامه في الأصول ولا فرق بين كون ما يقوم بها فعلاً اختياراً أو غيره حتى لو قال أنت طالق في مرضك أو وجعك أو صلاتك لم تطلق حتى تمرض أو تصلي، إما لأن في حرف بمعنى مع» أو لأن المرض ونحوه لما لم يصلح ظرفاً حمل على الشرط مجازاً لتصحيح كلام العاقل. وأشار في تلخيص الجامع إلى قاعدة هي الإضافة إن كانت إلى الموجود فإنه يتنجز كقوله أنت طالق في الدار ، وإن كانت إلى معدوم فإنه يتعلق كقوله في دخولك . وقيد بـ«في لأنه لو قال أنت طالق لدخولك الدار أو قال لحيضك تطلق للحال ولو قال أنت طالق بدخولك الدار أو بحيضك لا تطلق حتى تدخل الدار وتحيض. كذا في الخانية. وفي المحيط : لو قال أنت طالق في حيضك وهي حائض لم تطلق حتى تحيض أخرى لأنه عبارة عن درور الدم ونزوله لوقته فكان فعلاً فصار شرطاً كما في الدخول، والشرط يعتبر في المستقبل لا في الماضي. ولو قال أنت طالق في حيضة أو في حيضتك لم تطلق حتى تحيض وتطهر لأن الحيضة اسم للحيضة الكاملة لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سبايا أو طاس «إلا لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحيالي حتى يستبرئن بحيضة فأراد بها معنى كما لها اهـ . والحاصل أنه إن ذكر الحيضة بالتاء المثناة من فوق كان تعليقاً لطلاقها على الطهر من حيضة مستقبلة، وإن ذكره بغير تاء كان تعليقاً على رؤية الدم بشرط أن شرح التلخيص . ثم قال في المحيط : ولو قال أنت طالق في ثلاثة أيام طلقت للحال لأن تكلم بلفظ موضوع باعتبار العرف لمعنى معلوم فهو متكلم بحقيقة عرفية وبه يوجد صلاحية اللفظ لذلك واعتباره بقوله «اسقني الماء الخ) غير معتبر كما لا يخفى ا هـ . وكذا قال المقدسي : ولا يخفى أن اللفظ قوله : ( وإن كان الضمير مذكور الخ بأن قال فيه دخولك الدار والوقوع فيه للحال صريح أظهر لكونه عائداً إلى الطلاق. كذا في النهر.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Divorce. "Raji'ah and in Mecca or in the house: immediate; and if she enters Mecca: conditional." This is the meaning of the condition due to the suitability between them. If he said 'You are divorced in it (feminine) entering the house,' she is divorced immediately. Like this is stated in al-Muhit and al-Mi'raj. And he clarified in al-Dhakhira that when he mentions 'fi' without the letter 'ha', it refers to the first mentioned. Divorce and entering are not suitable as a container because it is an action, so it is made a condition, so the divorce becomes suspended on entering the house. When he mentions 'fi' with the letter 'ha', it becomes a description for the last mentioned, which is the entering, and divorce is not suitable as a container for entering, nor can divorce be made a condition also for entering, so the use as container and condition fails, so the word 'fi' is ignored, so the divorce falls by his saying 'You are divorced.' If the narration is with feminine 'ha', then it refers to the divorce instance; if the pronoun is masculine, it refers to the divorce (concept). It is not valid to suspend by it in his saying to a non-marriageable woman 'You are divorced in your marriage' so that even if he marries her, it does not occur because it is like a suspensive condition of suspension not arrangement. There is no difference between what stands as an action being voluntary or not, so that if he says 'You are divorced in your illness or your pain or your prayer,' she is not divorced until she becomes ill or prays. Either because 'fi' is in the meaning of 'with', or because illness and the like, since they are not suitable as a container, are interpreted as a condition metaphorically to correct the speech of a rational person. And he indicated in Talkhis al-Jami' a principle: the addition if it is to something existing, then it is immediate, like his saying 'You are divorced in the house'; if it is to something non-existent, then it is suspended, like his saying 'in your entering.' And it is restricted by 'fi', because if he said 'You are divorced for your entering the house' or 'for your menstruation,' she is divorced immediately. If he said 'You are divorced by your entering the house' or 'by your menstruation,' she is not divorced until she enters the house and menstruates. Like this in al-Khaniyya. In al-Muhit: If he said 'You are divorced in your menstruation' while she is menstruating, she is not divorced until she has another menstruation because it is an expression of the flowing and descending of blood at its time, so it is an action and becomes a condition like in entering, and the condition is considered in the future, not the past. If he said 'You are divorced in a menstruation' or 'in your menstruation (with ta),' she is not divorced until she menstruates and becomes pure because 'haydah' is the name for a complete menstruation due to his saying صلى الله عليه وسلم regarding captives: 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver their burden, nor with non-pregnant women until they are cleared by one menstruation,' meaning as for her. The conclusion: if he mentions 'haydah' with the 'ta', it is a suspension of her divorce on purity from a future menstruation; if he mentions it without 'ta', it is a suspension on seeing blood with the condition that... explanation of Talkhis. Then he said in al-Muhit: If he said 'You are divorced in three days,' she is divorced immediately because he spoke with a word placed according to custom for a known meaning, so he is speaking with a customary reality and by it the word is suitable for that, and consideration of it by his saying 'Give me water' etc. is not considered. And al-Maqdisi said similarly: it is not hidden that the word 'qawlihi' (his saying): 'If the pronoun is mentioned...' such that he said 'in it entering the house' and the occurrence is immediate, clear, more apparent because it refers to divorce. Like this in al-Nahr.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the legal effect of the particle 'في' in divorce statements. The author explains that when a husband says 'أنت طالق في الدار' (you are divorced in the house), the divorce is immediate because 'الدار' is an existing place, so 'في' functions as a container for the location. However, if he says 'أنت طالق في دخولك الدار' (you are divorced in your entering the house), the divorce is conditional upon entering, because 'دخول' is an action (a future event) and cannot be a container, so it is a condition. The key distinction is: if 'في' is followed by a noun that is an action (like دخول, حيض, مرض), the divorce is suspended (ta'liq); if followed by a noun of an existing place (like دار, مكة), the divorce is immediate (tanjiz). The text also discusses the variant with the feminine pronoun 'فيها' vs without. When 'فيها' is used, the 'ها' refers to the divorce instance, so the divorce is immediate because 'في' is linked to a previously mentioned location. The passage also covers exceptions: if the object is something that does not exist at the time of utterance, like 'في نكاحك' for a non-marriageable woman, it is a pure suspension and does not take effect even if she later becomes marriageable. The text cites multiple authorities (al-Muhit, al-Dhakhira, al-Khaniyya) to establish these rulings, and includes a hadith about istibra' with one menstruation to define 'حيضة' as a complete menstrual period. The overall legal reasoning is based on linguistic analysis (talil) to determine the intended meaning of a rational speaker.

Key Terms
في (fi): The Arabic particle meaning 'in', 'at', or 'during'; in divorce statements, its function depends on whether the object is an existing place (immediate) or a future action (conditional).
تنجيز (tanjiz): Immediate legal effect, as when the divorce takes effect at the moment of utterance without any condition.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the divorce on a future condition; the divorce does not take effect until the condition occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says 'أنت طالق في الدار' (you are divorced in the house), when does the divorce take effect?
A) Immediately
B) When she enters the house
C) It is invalid
D) Only after three menstrual cycles

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes immediate divorce (tanjiz) from conditional divorce (ta'liq) based on whether the object of 'في' is an existing place or a future action.

Divorce Attached to Time Expressions: Maji' vs Madiyy
Rulings on when divorce takes effect with future time indicators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effect of divorce statements attached to time expressions like 'fi maji'' and 'fi madiyy', and apply the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
'Maji'' refers to the first part of a time period; 'madiyy' refers to its entirety — divorce takes effect accordingly.

When a husband attaches a divorce statement to a future time, the precise wording determines when the divorce legally takes effect. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance based on the linguistic meanings of 'maji'' (coming) and 'madiyy' (passage). This lesson unpacks the key distinctions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time expression
Determine which phrase the husband used: 'ghadan', 'fi ghad', 'fi maji' yawm', 'fi madiyy yawm', 'fi maji' thalathat ayyam', or 'fi thalathat ayyam' (direct or agency).
Each expression triggers a different ruling.
2
Classify the expression as container (zarf) or condition (shart)
Words like 'fi ghad' act as a container (the time is a vessel for the divorce). 'Maji'' is an action, so it cannot be a container and becomes a condition. 'Madiyy' also acts as a condition but refers to passage of the whole period.
If it is a condition, the day of oath is not counted.
3
Apply the linguistic rule for 'maji''
'Maji' of a day means its first part. Thus, 'fi maji' yawm' triggers divorce at dawn of the next day. For multiple days, 'fi maji' thalathat ayyam' triggers at the beginning of the third day.
Analogous to how 'Friday came' means dawn rose.
4
Apply the linguistic rule for 'madiyy'
'Madiyy' refers to the full passage of the time period. If the husband swears after part of the day has passed, the remainder must be completed from the next day. 'Fi madiyy yawm' at 10 AM means divorce at 10 AM the next day.
If said at night, the divorce occurs at sunset of the third day for three days.
5
Distinguish direct pronouncement from agency
If the husband says 'Anti taliq fi thalathat ayyam', it is immediate (the divorce occurs at once). But if he appoints an agent to divorce her within three days, the agent may divorce her three separate times within that period.
Direct pronouncement does not extend over time; agency allows separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل

أنت طالق غداً أو في غد تطلق عند الصبح ونية العصر تصح في الثاني وفي الوقت يصلح ظرفاً لكونها طالقاً، ومتى طلقت في وقت طلقت في سائر الأوقات. ولو قال أنت طالق في مجيء ثلاثة أيام لم تطلق حتى يجيء اليوم الثالث لأن المجيء فعل فلم يصلح ظرفاً فصار شرطاً، ولا يحتسب باليوم الذي حلف فيه لأن الشروط تعتبر في المستقبل لا في الماضي، ومجيء اليوم يكون من أوله وقد مضى جزء أوله. ولو قال في مضي يوم تطلق في الغد في مثل تلك الساعة، ولو قال في مجيء يوم تطلق حين يطلع الفجر من الغد لأن المجيء عبارة عن مجيء أول جزئه. يقال جاء يوم الجمعة كما طلع الفجر، وجاء شهر رمضان كما هل الهلال وإن لم يجيء كله فصار كأنه قال أنت طالق إذا جاء أول جزء منه، فأما المضي فعبارة عن جميع أجزاء اليوم وقد وجد من حين حلف مضى بعض يوم كله فوجب ضرورة تتميمه من اليوم الثاني ليتحقق مضى جميع يوم ا وفي الجامع الكبير للصدر الشهيد : «في» للظرفية وتجعل شرطاً للتعذر إلى أن قال : ولو قال أنت طالق في ثلاثة أيام يتنجز والوكيل به يملك ثلاثاً متفرقة. قال بعد طلوع الشمس أنت طالق في مضي اليوم يقع عند غروبها، وفي مضي اليوم عند مجيء تلك الساعة، وكذا في مضي ثلاثة أيام، ولو قال ليلاً يقع عند غروب الشمس في الثالث ا.هـ. وصورة التوكيل به أن يقول لآخر طلق امرأتي في ثلاثة أيام والفرق بينهما أن الإيقاع لا يمتد فاقتضى التفريق بخلاف وصفها بالطلاق في الثلاثة .
Section: You are divorced tomorrow or on tomorrow - she is divorced at dawn. Intention of afternoon is valid in the second, and in time it is suitable as a container because she is divorced, and whenever she is divorced in a time, she is divorced in all times. If he said 'You are divorced in the coming of three days,' she is not divorced until the third day comes because 'coming' is an action, so it is not suitable as a container, so it becomes a condition. The day in which he swore is not counted because conditions are considered in the future, not the past. The coming of the day is from its beginning, and a part of its beginning has already passed. If he said 'in the passage of a day,' she is divorced tomorrow at the same hour. If he said 'in the coming of a day,' she is divorced at dawn of the next day because 'coming' is an expression of the coming of its first part. It is said 'Friday came' when dawn rises, and 'Ramadan came' when the crescent appears, even if it has not all come. So it is as if he said 'You are divorced if the first part of it comes.' As for 'passage', it is an expression for all parts of the day, and from the time he swore, some of the day has passed, so it is necessary to complete it from the second day to realize the passage of a full day. And in al-Jami' al-Kabir of al-Sadr al-Shahid: 'fi' is for container and is made a condition due to impossibility, until he said: if he said 'You are divorced in three days,' it is immediate, and the agent by it is empowered with three separate instances. He said after sunrise: 'You are divorced in the passage of the day,' it occurs at its sunset; and in the passage of the day (meaning the coming of that hour); similarly in the passage of three days. If he said at night, it occurs at sunset on the third. The form of agency for this is that he says to another: 'Divorce my wife in three days.' The difference between them is that the direct pronunciation does not extend, so it necessitates separation, unlike describing her with divorce in three.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This section ('فصل') deals with divorce statements attached to specific times. The author clarifies that when the husband says 'أنت طالق غداً' (you are divorced tomorrow), the divorce takes effect at dawn of the next day. If he says 'في غد' (on tomorrow), it also takes effect at dawn, but the husband's intention (e.g. intending afternoon) is considered valid in the latter. The key distinction is between phrases like 'في مجيء يوم' (in the coming of a day) and 'في مضي يوم' (in the passage of a day). 'مجيء' (coming) refers to the first part of the day, so the divorce occurs at dawn of the next day. 'مضي' (passage) refers to the entirety of the day, so if the oath is taken after sunrise, the day is partly passed, and the divorce will occur at sunset of the next day (or at the same hour the next day) to complete a full day. The text also differentiates between the husband's own pronouncement ('أنت طالق في ثلاثة أيام') where it is immediate, and when he makes another person an agent to divorce her within three days, where the agent has the power to divorce her three separate times within that period. This distinction is based on the principle that direct divorce does not extend over time, whereas agency allows for separation. The passage cites al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid to support these rulings.

Key Terms
مجيء (maji'): Coming or arrival; used for the first part of a day or month, not the whole duration.
مضي (madiyy): Passage or elapse; refers to the completion of all parts of a time period.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency; appointing another person to perform an act, here to issue divorce.
ظرف (zarf): Container; a word that indicates the time or place within which an action occurs.
شرط (shart): Condition; a future event upon which the divorce depends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) At the end of the day
C) At the beginning of the next day
D) Upon the arrival of the first part of the day after tomorrow

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a divorce is attached to a future time, the precise wording—whether 'maji'' (coming) or 'madiyy' (passage)—determines the exact moment the divorce takes effect, based on linguistic convention.

Divorce and Temporal Phrases: Zarf vs Shart
Expansion-probe: details how divorce takes effect for various temporal phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between temporal phrases that act as a container (zarf) and those that act as a condition (shart), and state when divorce takes effect for expressions like 'ghadan', 'fi maji'' and 'fi maddi'.

Core Idea
The time reference determines whether divorce is immediate or conditional: a container makes it immediate, an action makes it conditional.

A husband's utterance of divorce often includes a temporal reference. The Hanafi school carefully analyses whether the phrase indicates a container (zarf) for the divorce or sets a condition (shart) for its occurrence. This lesson unpacks the key expressions and their effects, drawn from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq.

Guided Path
1
Classify the temporal expression
Identify whether the phrase is a noun denoting a time (e.g., 'ghad') or a masdar denoting an action (e.g., 'maji''). The former is a container (zarf), the latter becomes a condition (shart).
The word 'fi' can introduce either, but the type of object determines the classification.
2
Apply the rule for containers
If the phrase is a container, the divorce takes effect at the earliest specified time. For 'ghadan' or 'fi ghadin', the divorce occurs at dawn of the next day, unless an intention for a later part (like 'asr') is made when using 'fi ghadin'.
Intention can modify the timing only for 'fi ghadin', not for 'ghadan'.
3
Apply the rule for conditions
If the phrase is an action (masdar) such as 'maji'' (coming) or 'maddi' (passing), it becomes a condition. The divorce occurs only when the action is fulfilled. For 'fi maji' thalathat ayyam', the divorce occurs at the beginning of the third day, not counting the day of utterance.
The day of the utterance is excluded because conditions apply to the future.
4
Distinguish between 'maji'' and 'maddi'
'Maji'' refers to the first part of a period (e.g., dawn of a day), so divorce occurs at that moment. 'Maddi' refers to the entire completion of a period, so for 'fi maddi yawm', the divorce occurs the next day at the same hour as the utterance.
This difference arises from the partil vs. whole nature of the masdar.
5
Note the special case of 'fi thalathati ayyam'
When used in a direct divorce (ta'liq), it is immediate. When used in a deputized divorce (tawkil), the agent may give three separate divorces over the three days. The distinction is because iqra' cannot extend over time, while tawkil allows description.
This is quoted from al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب الطلاق فصل أنت طالق غداً أو في غد تطلق عند الصبح ونية العصر تصح في الثاني وفي الوقت يصلح ظرفاً لكونها طالقاً، ومتى طلقت في وقت طلقت في سائر الأوقات. ولو قال أنت طالق في مجيء ثلاثة أيام لم تطلق حتى يجيء اليوم الثالث لأن المجيء فعل فلم يصلح ظرفاً فصار شرطاً، ولا يحتسب باليوم الذي حلف فيه لأن الشروط تعتبر في المستقبل لا في الماضي، ومجيء اليوم يكون من أوله وقد مضى جزء أوله. ولو قال في مضي يوم تطلق في الغد في مثل تلك الساعة، ولو قال في مجيء يوم تطلق حين يطلع الفجر من الغد لأن المجيء عبارة عن مجيء أول جزئه. يقال جاء يوم الجمعة كما طلع الفجر، وجاء شهر رمضان كما هل الهلال وإن لم يجيء كله فصار كأنه قال أنت طالق إذا جاء أول جزء منه، فأما المضي فعبارة عن جميع أجزاء اليوم وقد وجد من حين حلف مضى بعض يوم كله فوجب ضرورة تتميمه من اليوم الثاني ليتحقق مضى جميع يوم ا وفي الجامع الكبير للصدر الشهيد : «في» للظرفية وتجعل شرطاً للتعذر إلى أن قال : ولو قال أنت طالق في ثلاثة أيام يتنجز والوكيل به يملك ثلاثاً متفرقة. قال بعد طلوع الشمس أنت طالق في مضي اليوم يقع عند غروبها، وفي مضي اليوم عند مجيء تلك الساعة، وكذا في مضي ثلاثة أيام، ولو قال ليلاً يقع عند غروب الشمس في الثالث ا.هـ. وصورة التوكيل به أن يقول لآخر طلق امرأتي في ثلاثة أيام والفرق بينهما أن الإيقاع لا يمتد فاقتضى التفريق بخلاف وصفها بالطلاق في الثلاثة .
Chapter of Divorce, Section: 'You are divorced tomorrow' or 'on the morrow' – she is divorced at dawn; intention of 'asr is valid in the second; and the time serves as a container for her being divorced. Whenever she is divorced in a time, she is divorced in all times. If he said 'you are divorced in the coming of three days', she is not divorced until the third day comes because 'coming' is an action, so it is not suitable as a container and becomes a condition. The day in which he swore is not counted because conditions are considered for the future, not the past, and the coming of the day is from its beginning while part of its beginning has passed. If he said 'in the passing of a day', she is divorced tomorrow at that same hour. If he said 'in the coming of a day', she is divorced when the dawn breaks of the next day because 'coming' means the coming of its first part – it is said 'Friday came' when dawn breaks, and 'Ramadan came' when the crescent is sighted, even if not all of it has come. So it is as if he said 'you are divorced when the first part of it comes'. As for 'passing', it means all parts of the day, and from the time he swore, some of the day has passed, so it is necessary to complete it from the second day to realize the passing of a full day. In al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid: 'fi' is for containment and is made a condition due to impossibility, until he said: if he said 'you are divorced in three days', it takes effect immediately, and the agent (wakeel) is empowered to give three separate divorces. He said: after sunrise 'you are divorced in the passing of the day' occurs at sunset; 'in the passing of the day' at the coming of that hour; similarly 'in the passing of three days'; if he said at night, it occurs at sunset on the third. End. The form of deputizing is that he says to another 'divorce my wife in three days', and the difference between them is that the actual divorce (iqra') does not extend, so it necessitates separation, unlike describing her with divorce in three.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, explaining how divorce tied to temporal expressions takes effect. The key distinction is between words that denote a container (zarf) like 'fi' with a noun that is a time (like 'ghad'), and words that denote an action (like 'maji'' or 'maddi'). 'Ghadan' and 'fi ghadin' both result in divorce at dawn of the next day, but 'fi ghadin' allows intention for a later part of the day (like 'asr). If the wife is already divorced at a time, she is divorced at all times (i.e., the divorce is effective at that moment). For 'fi maji' thalathat ayyam', since 'maji'' is an action, it cannot be a container; it becomes a condition, so the divorce occurs exactly when the third day begins, not counting the day of utterance. For 'fi maddi yawm', 'passing' refers to the full completion of a day, so the divorce occurs the next day at the same hour. The text quotes al-Sadr al-Shahid clarifying that 'fi' in 'fi thalathati ayyam' for a direct divorce (ta'liq) makes it immediate, but for a deputized divorce (tawkil), the agent can give three separate divorces within the three days. The difference is that direct iqra' cannot be extended over time, so it must be immediate, whereas describing her with divorce (as in tawkil) allows the agent to space them out.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A container: a noun that serves as the time or place in which an action occurs, allowing the divorce to be effective at that time.
شرط (shart): A condition: when the expression is an action (like 'maji''), it becomes a condition for the divorce to occur, not a container.
مجيء (maji'): The arrival or coming of something; treated as a verb-based noun (masdar) indicating an action, thus a condition.
مضي (maddi): The passing or elapsing of time; refers to the full completion of a period, thus requires waiting until the entire day passes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his wife 'anti taliq fi maji' thalathat ayyam'. When does the divorce take effect?
A) Immediately
B) At the end of the third day
C) At the beginning of the third day
D) After three full days from the utterance

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, divorce tied to a temporal phrase is either immediate (if the phrase is a container) or conditional (if it is an action), with precise timing determined by the linguistic classification of the phrase.

Ta'qit in Divorce: The Principle and the Madhhab Dispute
Explains that divorce cannot be time-limited and contrasts with contracts that accept ta'qit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why divorce cannot be time-limited (ta'qit) and apply the rule that 'ila' means 'after' using the Hanafi analogy with tadbir.

Core Idea
Divorce cannot be time-limited; the preposition 'ila' means 'after' not 'until'.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sets out the Hanafi rule that divorce does not accept ta'qit (time-limiting), in contrast to many other contracts. A key inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik arises: if a divorce is tied to an inevitable future time, does it take effect immediately? The Hanafi proof is the analogy with tadbir (manumission after death). The passage then surveys a wide range of contracts to show where ta'qit is accepted or rejected, providing a comprehensive systematic view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central rule and the dispute
First, note the foundational rule: divorce cannot be time-limited (ta'qit). Then identify the opposing view of Malik, who holds that if the future time is inevitable (like sunrise), the divorce should take effect immediately. Understand the practical difference.
The rule applies to all formulations like 'anti taliq ila shahr' or 'anti taliq ghadan'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof using tadbir
The Hanafi response to Malik is based on analogy (qiyas) with tadbir: a master says 'you are free after my death'. Death is inevitable but the effect is delayed until death. Similarly, an inevitable future time does not force immediate effect. Examine this analogy critically.
Tadbir is a well-known Hanafi example; the inevitability of the condition does not necessitate immediate legal effect.
3
Apply the rule to the phrase 'ila' meaning 'after'
Because divorce does not accept ta'qit, the preposition 'ila' (up to) in divorce contexts is interpreted as 'after' (ba'd). For example, 'anti taliq ila 'asharat ayyam' means she is divorced after ten days, not that the divorce lasts ten days.
This is a distinct Hanafi linguistic interpretation; other contexts may treat 'ila' differently.
4
Survey other contracts for ta'qit acceptance
The passage lists numerous contracts: manumission (like divorce), suretyship (disputed), option of the hand (immediate but expires), sale (deferment of price), agency (accepts), hire, muzara'ah, partnership (like hire), sulh and division (invalid with ta'qit), ibra' (like divorce but intention matters), iqrar (conditional), slave's permission (no), tahkim and qada (accept). Understand the pattern.
Contracts that are intrinsically continuous (hire, partnership) accept ta'qit as a natural time limit; divorce is a single event and thus does not.
5
Note the correction about missing word
The passage ends with a note that in al-Bazzaziyyah the word 'la' (not) is omitted or a noun is missing. This highlights the importance of textual accuracy in fiqh transmission.
Such corrections are common in sharh literature.

يحتمل التأقيت فتكون هذه إضافة للإيقاع إلى ما بعد الستة اهـ . فالحكم موافق والعلة مخالفة لما هنا وفي البزازية في الأمر باليد بعد أن ذكر أن الأمر يحتمل التوقيت بخلاف الطلاق حتى لو قال أنت طالق إلى عشرة Section: Then know that divorce is time-limited (ta'qit). Ar-Ramli said in al-Walwalijiyyah: A man said to his wife 'you are divorced' from her existence... [long aside on classification of sciences]... His statement: 'You are divorced tomorrow or on the morrow' – she is divorced at dawn because in the first he described her with divorce in all of it, since all of it is what is called tomorrow, so the first part is determined due to no competition; in the second he described her in a part of it, and he conveyed that when he adds it to a time, it does not occur immediately – this is the statement of Shafi'i and Ahmad. Malik said: it occurs immediately if the time inevitably arrives, like saying 'if the sun rises' or 'when tomorrow enters in Ramadan' and the like; and this is invalid by analogy with tadbir (manumission after death), for death comes inevitably but does not take effect immediately. That is from al-Mi'raj. Then know that divorce is time-limited; so if he says 'you are divorced up to ten days', it occurs after ten days, and 'ila' here means 'after'. Manumission and suretyship up to a month are like divorce; regarding the latter, according to the second (Abu Yusuf?), he is a surety immediately, but the fatwa is that he is a surety after a month. The command (amr) regarding the hand (option) up to ten days: the option is in her hand immediately and expires after ten days; if he intended it to be in her hand after ten days, that is not accepted judicially. Sale up to a month is a deferment of the price; agency accepts time-limiting, so if he acts after the time, it is invalid. In hire (ijara) up to a month, the period immediately following the contract is determined and ends after it; similarly for muzara'ah; partnership (shirkah) up to a month is like hire; sulh up to a month and division up to it are invalid; ibra' up to a month is like divorce, except if he says 'I intended delay', then it is a deferment. Acknowledgement (iqrar) up to two months: if the acknowledgee confirms him, the term is established; if he denies him, the property is due immediately and the statement is his. Permission of a slave does not accept ta'qit; arbitration (tahkim) and qada accept ta'qit. Prohibition of the agent from selling for a day accepts ta'qit. This summary clarifies what is time-limited and what is not; I mention it here due to its many benefits; it is mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah in the section on the option of the hand. There from oaths: 'you are such and such if tomorrow comes' is a vow; 'you are such and such tomorrow' is not a vow because it is an addition (idafah). Divorce added to two times takes effect at the earlier of them; divorce suspended on two actions takes effect at the later. 'Up to a year' occurs after the year because divorce does not admit ta'qit, so this is an addition of the iqa' to after the year. So the ruling is consistent but the reason is contrary to what is here. In al-Bazzaziyyah in the option of the hand, after mentioning that the command admits time-limiting unlike divorce, so if he says 'you are divorced up to ten days', 'ila' means 'after' because delaying the occurrence is impossible, so he delayed the iqa'; if he intended it to occur immediately, it does occur. So it is established that the word 'la' (not) is omitted by mistake or there is a deleted noun, i.e., 'the iqa' of divorce'. Ponder his statement 'except if he said I intended delay, then it is a deferment'; the author has a discussion on this that will come in the chapter on the option of the hand. His statement: 'and divorce added to two times' – i.e., both future; if one is present, its explanation will come at his saying 'and on the day tomorrow'.
