Distinguishing Addition from Condition in Divorce Timing
Expansion of the ruling with talil (reasoning) differentiating idafa and shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ambiguous divorce timing and explain the distinction between idafa (addition) and shart (condition) with legal reasoning.

Core Idea
When two future times are mentioned with 'or', the divorce occurs at the first; a condition suspends the divorce until fulfillment.

The wording of divorce is critical in Hanafi law. A husband's utterance may be immediate, added to a future time, or conditioned on an event. This lesson unpacks a key rule: when two times are linked with 'or', the first is effective, and the second is redundant. But if a condition is used, the divorce is delayed. We will explore the legal reasoning behind this distinction, including the concepts of tanjiz, idafa, and shart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pronouncing divorce with a time reference. The ruling: when a husband says 'you are divorced today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today', the divorce occurs in the first time mentioned, immediately. If he says 'you are divorced today when tomorrow comes', it is conditional and occurs at dawn tomorrow.
The key is whether the second time is an addition (idafa) or a condition (shart).
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator uses a qiyas khafi (istihsan) based on the effective cause: in 'today tomorrow', the second time is redundant because if she is divorced today, she is also divorced tomorrow. In 'today when tomorrow comes', the condition changes the ruling by suspending the divorce.
The proof is not a direct text but analogical reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause ('illa) is the presence of a condition that changes the default immediacy. Without a condition, the first time is taken as immediate and the second is ignored. With a condition, the divorce is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.
This distinguishes between idafa (mere specification of time) and shart (suspension).
4
Analyze the distinction between idafa and shart
The commentator notes that scholars were asked for the difference. One argument: in shart, 'today' specifies the time of suspension, not occurrence; in idafa, it specifies occurrence. But the commentator suggests this is insufficient. The real difference is that idafa does not alter the immediacy of the first part, while shart suspends it.
This is a nuanced point of Hanafi usul al-fiqh applied to talaq.
5
Apply to a compound utterance
If the husband says 'you are divorced today and when tomorrow comes', the conjunction 'and' makes the condition apply only to the second part, resulting in two divorces: one now and one tomorrow. This is because the immediate part cannot be attached to a condition.
This shows how the presence of a conjunction changes the analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وفي اليوم غداً أو غداً اليوم يعتبر الأول أي يقع الطلاق في أول الوقتين تفوّه به عند عدم النية ؛ أما الأول فلأنه نجزه فلا يقع متأخراً إلى وقت في المستقبل ولا يعتبر لإضافة أخرى لأنه لا حاجة إليه لأنها إذا طلقت اليوم كانت غداً كذلك، وأما الثاني فلأنه مضافاً بعده فلا يكون منجزاً بعده بل لو اعتبر كان تطليقاً آخر، وإنما وصفها بواحدة فلزم إلغاء الثاني ضرورة، ولا يمكن جعله نسخاً للأول لأن النسخ إنما يكون بكلام مستيد متراخ وهو منتف . قيد بقوله اليوم غداً » لأنه إذا قال أنت طالق اليوم إذا جاء غد لا تطلق . إلا بطلوع الفجر فتوقف المنجز لاتصاله بغير الأول بالآخر، وقد جعلوا الشرط مغيراً للأول دون الإضافة وقد طولبوا بالفرق بينهما، وما ذكروا من أن اليوم في الشرط لبيان وقت التعليق لا لبيان وقت الوقوع وفي الإضافة لبيان وقت الوقوع لا يفيد فرقاً. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم وإذا جاء غد طلقت واحدة للحال وأخرى في الغد لأن المجيء شرط معطوف على الإيقاع والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه والموقع للحال لا يكون متعلقاً بشرط فلا بد وأن يكون المتعلق تطليقة أخرى. كذا في المحيط .
His statement: (And 'today tomorrow' or 'tomorrow today', the first is considered) meaning the divorce occurs in the first of the two times when he uttered it, in the absence of intention. As for the first, because he made it immediate, so it does not occur later at a future time, and no other addition is considered because there is no need for it, since if she is divorced today, she is also divorced tomorrow. As for the second, because it is added afterwards, so it is not immediate afterwards; rather if it were considered, it would be another divorce. And he only described her with one divorce, so canceling the second is necessary. And it cannot be made an abrogation of the first because abrogation only is by a separate later speech, which is absent. He restricted with his statement 'today tomorrow' because if he said 'you are divorced today when tomorrow comes', she is not divorced except at the break of dawn, thus the immediate is suspended because it is connected to other than the first by the second. And they made the condition changing the first but not the addition. And they were asked for the difference between them. And what they mentioned that 'today' in the condition is to specify the time of suspension not the time of occurrence, and in the addition to specify the time of occurrence, does not give a difference. And if he said 'you are divorced today and when tomorrow comes', she is divorced one now and another tomorrow, because the coming is a condition conjoined to the occurrence, and the conjoined is not the conjoined to, and what occurs now is not attached to a condition, so it must be that the attached is another divorce. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This is an expansion probe by the commentator of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. He explains the reasoning behind the rule: when two times are mentioned with 'or', the first is effective because the divorce is made immediate (tanjiz). If a condition is used (e.g., 'if tomorrow comes'), the divorce is suspended. The difference between addition (idafa) and condition (shart) is that addition specifies the time of occurrence, while condition specifies the time of suspension. However, the commentator notes that this distinction does not fully satisfy. The passage then gives a different scenario: 'you are divorced today and when tomorrow comes' – here, due to the conjunction 'and' (wa), the condition applies only to the second part, resulting in two divorces. This commentary relies on al-Muhit, a primary Hanafi source.

Key Terms
تنجيز (tanjiz): Making the divorce immediate and effective at the moment of utterance
إضافة (idafa): Adding a future time to the divorce, e.g., 'you are divorced tomorrow'
شرط (shart): A condition that suspends the divorce until its fulfillment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'you are divorced today tomorrow', when does the divorce occur?
A) Today
B) Tomorrow
C) Both today and tomorrow
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
The distinction between idafa (addition) and shart (condition) is crucial in determining the timing of divorce; the former does not affect immediacy, while the latter suspends it.

Effect of Conjunction 'Waw' on Timing of Divorce
Expands the Hanafi rule on conjunction in time-linked divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for the effect of the conjunction 'and' (waw) when a divorce is tied to multiple times, distinguishing between present and future mentions and accounting for intention.

Core Idea
When times are linked with 'waw', order determines count: present first = one, future first = two.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on a concise ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the effect of the conjunction 'waw' when a husband pronounces divorce tied to two or more times. The key principle from al-Muhit is that if both times are future, the divorce occurs at the earlier time to cover both. However, if one time is present and the other future, the order in which they are mentioned changes the number of divorces. The passage also addresses the role of intention (niyyah) and notes a disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the times mentioned
Determine whether each time is present (already occurring at the moment of utterance) or future. For example, 'today' is present if said during the day; 'tomorrow' is future.
The time of utterance matters. For 'night' and 'day', the present time depends on when the statement is made.
2
Check the order of times after the conjunction
Note which time appears first and which appears second. The rule applies to the sequence: first mentioned (ma'tuf 'alayh) and second mentioned (ma'tuf).
The conjunction 'waw' does not imply sequence in Arabic grammar, but the Hanafi school gives legal weight to the order.
3
Apply the base rule from al-Muhit
If both times are future, the divorce occurs at the earlier time, counting as one divorce. If one is present and one is future: if the present is mentioned first, one divorce; if the future is mentioned first, two divorces.
The two divorces are: one at the first (future) time and one at the second (present) time because they cannot both occur at the same moment.
4
Consider intention (niyyah)
If the husband intended additional divorces, they multiply accordingly. For example, if he intended one for today and one for tomorrow, and he said 'today and tomorrow', two divorces occur despite the base rule.
Intention can override the default rule. However, if no intention, the default applies.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with Zufar
When three times are mentioned with 'and' (e.g., 'tomorrow and today and the day after'), the Hanafi position (from al-Muhit) is that three divorces occur if the woman is consummated. Zufar disagreed.
The practical difference affects the count and thereby the finality of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم وغداً أو أول النهار وآخره لا يقع عليه إلا واحدة إلا إذا نوى أخرى فيتعدد وفي المسألة الثانية بينهما فرق فإنه لو قال أنت طالق اليوم وغداً وقعت واحدة، ولو قال أنت طالق غداً واليوم وقعت ثنتان للمغابرة بين المعطوف والمعطوف عليه عند الاحتياج، وهو في الثانية دون الأولى. وكذا لو قال أمس واليوم فهي ثنتان لأن الواقع في اليوم لا يكون واقعاً في الأمس فاقتضى أخرى، ولو قال اليوم وأمس فهي واحدة مثل قوله اليوم وغداً. كذا في المحيط فيه : لو قال أنت طالق غداً واليوم وبعد غد والمرأة مدخول بها يقع ثلاثاً خلافاً لزفر وفي الخانية : أنت طالق اليوم وبعد غد طلقت ثنتان في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقيدنا بعدم النية لأنه لو نوى في الأولى أن يقع عليها اليوم واحدة وغداً واحدة صبح ووقعت ثنتان. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم وغداً وبعد غد تقع واحدة بلا نية، فإن نوى ثلاثاً متفرقة على ثلاثة أيام وقعن كذلك. واستفيد من المسألتين أنه لو قال بالنهار أنت طالق بالليل والنهار يقع عليه تطليقتان ولو قال بالنهار والليل تقع واحدة، ولو كان بالليل انعكس الحكم. كذا في التنقيح للمحبوبي . وعلى هذا فما ذكره الشارح من أنه لو قال أنت طالق آخر النهار وأوله تطلق ثنتين ولو قال أنت طالق أول النهار وآخره تطلق واحدة مقيد بما إذا كانت هذه المقالة في أول النهار، فلو كانت في آخر النهار انعكس الحكم. وفي المحيط الأصل أن الطلاق متى أضيف إلى وقتين مستقبلين نزل في أولهما ليصير واقعاً فيهما، وإن كان أحد الوقتين كائناً والآخر مستقبلاً وبينهما حرف العطف، فإن بدأ بالكائن وقع طلاق واحد في أولهما، وإن بدأ بالمستقبل وقع طلاقان ا هـ .
And if he said 'you are divorced today and tomorrow' or 'the beginning of the day and its end', only one divorce occurs unless he intended another, then they multiply. In the second issue there is a difference: if he said 'you are divorced today and tomorrow', one divorce; if he said 'you are divorced tomorrow and today', two divorces, because of the difference between the conjoined and the conjoined-to when there is need, and that is in the second not the first. Similarly, if he said 'yesterday and today', two divorces because what occurs today does not occur yesterday, so another is required; if he said 'today and yesterday', one divorce like saying 'today and tomorrow'. Thus in al-Muhit. In it: if he said 'you are divorced tomorrow and today and the day after' and the woman is consummated, three divorces occur, contrary to Zufar. And in al-Khaniyyah: 'you are divorced today and the day after' — two divorces according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and we restrict it to absence of intention because if he intended in the first that one divorce falls today and one tomorrow morning, then two fall. And if he said 'you are divorced today and tomorrow and the day after', one divorce without intention; if he intended three separate over three days, they fall accordingly. It is derived from the two issues that if he said during the day 'you are divorced at night and day', two divorces occur; if he said 'at day and night', one; if it was at night, the ruling reverses. Thus in al-Tanqih by al-Mahbubi. Based on this, what the commentator mentioned that if he says 'you are divorced at the end of the day and its beginning', she is divorced twice; if he says 'you are divorced at the beginning of the day and its end', she is divorced once, is restricted to when this statement is at the beginning of the day; if at the end of the day, the ruling reverses. And in al-Muhit, the principle: when divorce is added to two future times, it occurs in the first of them so that it becomes effective in both; and if one time is present and the other future and between them there is a conjunction, if he begins with the present, one divorce occurs at the first of them, and if he begins with the future, two divorces.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of using the conjunction 'and' (waw) to connect two or more time references in a divorce pronouncement. The key principle, stated at the end from al-Muhit, is that when two future times are mentioned, the divorce occurs at the earlier time to cover both. However, when one time is present and the other future, the order matters: if he begins with the present, only one divorce occurs (because the present already includes the future?); if he begins with the future, two divorces occur (one now and one later). Examples are given with 'today and tomorrow', 'yesterday and today', 'night and day', and 'beginning and end of the day'. The ruling depends on the time of utterance. There is a known ikhtilaf with Zufar regarding three times. The passage also discusses the effect of intention (niyyah). This is an expansion on the basic rule from the matn.

Key Terms
المعطوف (al-ma'tuf): The conjoined term (the second time mentioned)
المعطوف عليه (al-ma'tuf 'alayh): The term to which something is conjoined (the first time mentioned)
الكائن (al-ka'in): The present time (already occurring)
المستقبل (al-mustaqbal): The future time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says during the day 'you are divorced at night and day', how many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
When a divorce is tied to two times with 'and', the order matters: present first = one divorce, future first = two divorces, and intention can modify the count.
